# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Designed specifically for image-classification problems by 
 Alex Krishevski in 2012. ^SfHybqUX

Similar to Simple Peceptron, AlexNet uses bounded layers of "neurons",
but with 2 main distinctions:
- Instead of, actually, neurons, we use feature maps
- Instead of applying simple weights to each neuron, we apply a whole
kernel to calculate next layer

Before observing an overrall CNN example, we should get known to 
2 new instances: kernels and pooling layers ^TJI3t5T5

OVERALL SIGHT: ^VNll9HSG

The main idea is to successively apply kernels and poolings
to reduce original dimension space (typically to 1/1/n), then flatten the
output and apply a Simple Fully Connected layer perceptron for
classification 
 ^l7DpeuqL

KERNELS ^VT4tfJFW

POOLING ^L5NT7gg8

Average, Max/Min Pooling is used to reduce channel`s dimensions
(usually by 2^k times), helping NN to generalize features better and 
reduce number of trainable parameters. ^u213NIwk

* pool_size = (int, int) is a parameter controlling pooling scope size
* stride = (int, int) is a parameter controlling amount of movement, 
adjusting pooling scope
by stride[0] from left to right and
by stride[1] from top to bottom ^ytDhxxXH

* kernel_size: (int, int), specifying the size of the convolution window.
* strides: (int, int), specifying the stride length of the convolution. 
* padding: string, either "valid" or "same" (case-insensitive). 
"valid" means no padding. 
"same" results in padding evenly to the left/right or up/down of the input. 
When padding="same" and strides=1, the output has the same size as the input. ^WmF19Iem

p ^94ReNhCh

## Element Links
BdaQrIgx: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CEUNTRdLhKk&t=1043s
